    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4008014730198874437">De zestienjarige Dolf uit Amstelveen geeft zich op als proefkonijn: hij zal door een materie-transmitter teruggeflitst worden naar de Middeleeuwen om daar één middag een kijkje te nemen. Maar door een foute berekening komt hij in het jaar 1212 terecht in een Kinderkruistocht die net uit Keulen is vertrokken en niet op het riddertoernooi in Montgivray in Midden-Frankrijk da</span>
  <span id="freeText4008014730198874437" style="display:none">De zestienjarige Dolf uit Amstelveen geeft zich op als proefkonijn: hij zal door een materie-transmitter teruggeflitst worden naar de Middeleeuwen om daar één middag een kijkje te nemen. Maar door een foute berekening komt hij in het jaar 1212 terecht in een Kinderkruistocht die net uit Keulen is vertrokken en niet op het riddertoernooi in Montgivray in Midden-Frankrijk dat hij zo graag wilde bijwonen.<br /><br />Verbijsterd ziet hij duizenden gelovige – en vooral goedgelovige – kinderen, aan wie wonderen zijn beloofd, zingend aan hem voorbijtrekken. Zij zijn van plan met hun blote handen het Heilige Land van de Saracenen te bevrijden.<br /><br />Om vijf uur diezelfde middag moet Dolf weer op de afgesproken plek staan om teruggeflitst te worden naar de twintigste eeuw – tenminste, als er niets fout gaat…<br /><br />Lengte: 11 uur 26 minuten</span>
  <a data-text-id="4008014730198874437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I didn't remember the story though, but I really enjoyed reading it now as a grown up. The story is great with lots of adventure in it and you learn a lot of the history. It is written in a way that you want to keep reading because you want to know what will happen next. It gets 5 points because of how well it is written, and how I loved it.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567431438i/28088694._SX540_.jpg' width='350' height='230' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book is in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936332.1001_Children_s_Books_You_Must_Read_Before_You_Grow_Up' title='1001 Children's Books You Must Read Before You Grow Up by Julia Eccleshare' rel='nofollow noopener'>1001 Children's Books You Must Read Before You Grow Up</a></span>

<div id="review_112558057" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112558057" />
    <a title="LenaLena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4033763-lenalena"><img alt="LenaLena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362798973p2/4033763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112558057?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LenaLena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LenaLena" href="/user/show/4033763-lenalena">LenaLena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781886910263" href="/book/show/974324.Crusade_in_Jeans">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033763-lenalena?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033763-lenalena?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4033763-lenalena?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112558057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16531722559235247748">I am not sure I have the words to adequately describe how much I've loved this book and still love this book. My 4th grade teacher started reading this to our class back in '78 or so. About two chapters in I couldn't stand his slow pace anymore, got the book out of the library and plowed through it in a day or two. I have reread this book so many times I have long lost count and even as an adult I reread it every few years. My battered '83 copy, without a spine and held together by yellowing sco</span>
  <span id="freeText16531722559235247748" style="display:none">I am not sure I have the words to adequately describe how much I've loved this book and still love this book. My 4th grade teacher started reading this to our class back in '78 or so. About two chapters in I couldn't stand his slow pace anymore, got the book out of the library and plowed through it in a day or two. I have reread this book so many times I have long lost count and even as an adult I reread it every few years. My battered '83 copy, without a spine and held together by yellowing scotch tape, now sits on my bookshelf in California, half a world away from where I first read it. This one goes with me whenever I move.<br /><br />The books tells the story of how Dolf, a twentieth century boy, gets stranded in a children's crusade in the 13th century and travels with the crusade from Germany, over the Alps, to Italy. Along the way he transforms the crusade from a ragtag band of rabble, in which the smallest and weakest children perish, into a well organized troupe that takes care of their own. He battles epidemic outbreaks of disease, bandits, nature, accusations of heresy, superstition and the medieval mindset. The author, one of my personal holy trinity of 70's Dutch children's lit (Thea Beckman, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26747.Jan_Terlouw" title="Jan Terlouw" rel="nofollow noopener">Jan Terlouw</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/148470.Tonke_Dragt" title="Tonke Dragt" rel="nofollow noopener">Tonke Dragt</a>) does an excellent job describing the grueling nature of the journey, the good and the bad, providing a touching experience for the reader, without having Dolf wallow in angst and agony every other page. <br /><br />When netgalley offered the English translation, I jumped on it. It was about time for another reread anyway. It was a little weird that many of the names had been changed. Rudolf Wega from Amstelveen is now Rudolf Hefting from Amsterdam, Mariecke is Maria, Dom Johannes Dom Augustus etc. But okay, pandering to the English inability to deal with foreign names, I can live with that. <br /><br />What was more disturbing is that the story seemed a little flat... Was I finally too old for this story? Did I know it too well? Then I noticed some sentence structures were a bit clunky. ('All that they had so far suffered would pale beside the horrors that awaited them in the mountains' and 'My friend here is rather fond of seeing off bears'). Maybe it needed some more editing from a native English speaker? <br /><br />Then, when Mariecke/Maria returns from gathering herbs with a bunch of 'henchmen' and I was wondering when she had become a villain needing henchmen, I decided to get out the original. <br /><br />Well, no wonder the story felt a bit flat.... <br /><br />Here is a passage that describes Dolf coming into the camp on the evening after the first day the 7000 children had to cross a mountain pass: <br /><br /><i>For indeed, he now felt responsible for the children's crusade. For every accident, for every death he blamed himself. And today that burden had proved heavy. Through the tortuous miles of the gorge he had walked with but the one thought that he must get them all through safely. But he had failed. Right in front of his eyes he had seen a child fall into the stream and be carried away by the torrent. For two hours he had been frantically digging into the rock-slide with nothing but a stick and his bare hands – only to find one dead child. He had carried on his back children who had fallen down and when they were rested set them on their feet and picked up another. Had they all reached the end of the gorge safely? He could not tell. Dolf knew that Leonardo, like himself, was not sleeping. </i><br /><br />Now the same passage in the original, translated by me (not a native English speaker, so cut me some slack).<br /><br /><i>Because it had come to this: he felt completely responsible for the children's crusade. Every accident, every death, he held himself accountable for. And today he'd had his share. All the difficult miles through the gorge he had had but one thought: 'I have to get all of them them through this safely.' But he had failed. Right before his eyes he had seen a child fall into the raging creek, swept away by the torrent to get smashed onto a rock in the riverbed. He had spent two hours frantically digging into a rock-slide with nothing but a stick and his bare hands, only to finally uncover a dead child. How many others were still buried, he could not guess, he only knew he'd lost them. He had helped crying children clamber over rocks and he had seen the ox die. He had sucked out a snake bite, uncertain if the snake had been venomous. And where was that little guy now? He had carried children on his back that had fallen down. He had put them down and picked up others. Had they all made it to the end of the gorge? Hadn't they accidentally left one behind? He had not been able to keep up with them all. Fifty, maybe a hundred children he knew by name and face. The thousands of others were just children, entrusted to his care. He could not tell them apart, there were too many of them. <br />	The chaos in the camp shocked him. Night was threatening. The sky was still clouded, even if it had stopped raining and it was black as pitch. The still valley was rustling with hidden life, with stealthy dangers. A large fire would keep predators at bay, but the fires were going out. The tired wood gatherers had only gathered enough to cook dinner on. Packs of wolves, attracted to the smell of cooked meat and gnawed bones were silently stalking the perimeter of the camp. Dolf could see their eyes light up when they came close. Staggering through the camp he heard a child scream, but before he had reached the spot, silence had set back in. What had happened? <br />	Occasionally, an arrow shot through the air, loosened by one of the orderlies. One time, Dolf heard the whining flight of an animal that had been shot. But there weren't enough orderlies, they fell asleep or nobody came to relieve them. Exhaustion and despair were sapping Dolf's strength. He had put Maria/Mariecke and a number of small children safely in the middle of the group, near the tent. And he knew that Leonardo was not sleeping either, but was doing his utmost to keep the camp safe, just like he was. </i><br /><br />OMFG.... <br /><br />Somebody do a new translation of this book please, so I can stop crying. <br /><br />So, the 5 stars are for the Dutch original. I have no words, or stars, for the English translation. I saw that the this edition still averages between 4 and 5 stars from other reviewers on goodreads, though, which shows you that a good story is pretty much indestructible, even when butchered in the translation. But, damn, it hurts. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16531722559235247748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113619840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113619840" />
    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113619840?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781886910263" href="/book/show/974324.Crusade_in_Jeans">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who don’t mind a different take on religious history; those who like time travel stories</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=orphaned-and-quasi-orphaned-kids">orphaned-and-quasi-orphaned-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=z2010">z2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=readbooks-female-author-or-illust">readbooks-female-author-or-illust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=zz-4star">zz-4star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113619840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16839226657213933864">This ended up being a very satisfying read. I’m sure if I’d read this at age 10, it would have been a 5 star book for me. I would have particularly enjoyed the episodic adventures of Dolf and the children when I was that age.<br/><br/>I very quickly had to suspend my adult sensibilities major disbelief and try to put myself back to my 9 or 10 or 11 year old self, eager for a fantasy novel. I’m not talking about the time travel aspect, but there is no way that scientists, let alone a father, would let happ</span>
  <span id="freeText16839226657213933864" style="display:none">This ended up being a very satisfying read. I’m sure if I’d read this at age 10, it would have been a 5 star book for me. I would have particularly enjoyed the episodic adventures of Dolf and the children when I was that age.<br /><br />I very quickly had to suspend my adult sensibilities major disbelief and try to put myself back to my 9 or 10 or 11 year old self, eager for a fantasy novel. I’m not talking about the time travel aspect, but there is no way that scientists, let alone a father, would let happen what happened at the beginning of this book, especially not in that hasty and ill thought out manner. <br /><br />I became so curious so I had to look up the history, and I found living history. Interesting. Interesting take the book has too. A friend when we were fifteen was interested in children’s crusades and I think that they deepened her Christian beliefs; I wonder what she’d think about new thinking on the subject. <br /><br />This particular story and its opinions felt very 1970s to me. The author wrote it and it was published first in the Netherlands (great translation, I think) but it did not have a foreign feel to me.<br /><br />I liked how the religious-not religious and those from different centuries learned from one another.<br /><br />As a non-religious person I liked that Dolf was not religious but wondered throughout the book if that would last, and I also wondered about whether the whole big picture would change. I loved how that was resolved. It felt so real that only the time travel aspect felt like speculative fiction. I do wonder how some religious Christians would feel about this children’s novel, and I wonder if it’s on any banned lists.<br /><br />Something I did not like was when a narrator comes in occasionally to explain what the Middle Ages were like; the information is interesting and I’m glad it was included, but I wish it had been incorporated in a less clumsy way. Another negative was the extremely abrupt ending, reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/895953.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Series___1_" title="A Wrinkle in Time (Time Series, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wrinkle in Time</a>, but I forgive it for that. In fact, it’s fun to imagine the reactions of some of the characters in the book after the what happens at the end of the story in the book. <br /><br />I read this for the International Books Club at the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/188.Children_s_Books" rel="nofollow noopener">Children's Books group</a>. It's the November book, so I'm ahead for once!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16839226657213933864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2765157570" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2765157570" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2765157570?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783423713115" href="/book/show/4952264-kreuzzug-in-jeans">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=translations">translations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=time-travel-time-slip">time-travel-time-slip</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2765157570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13454398599380254794">After rather totally stalling and generally feeling mostly massively annoyed with the narrative flow of the anonymous English language translation of Thea Beckman's 1973 time travel novel <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u> (<u>Crusade in Jeans</u>) when I was trying to read the latter about nine or so years ago and became increasingly frustrated with and by how everything in the English rendition seems to feel distractingly distant and that the text also moves along at best awkwardly and very often feeling lik</span>
  <span id="freeText13454398599380254794" style="display:none">After rather totally stalling and generally feeling mostly massively annoyed with the narrative flow of the anonymous English language translation of Thea Beckman's 1973 time travel novel <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u> (<u>Crusade in Jeans</u>) when I was trying to read the latter about nine or so years ago and became increasingly frustrated with and by how everything in the English rendition seems to feel distractingly distant and that the text also moves along at best awkwardly and very often feeling like one is actually reading not just a translation but yes indeed a painfully slow literal word-for-word rendition of Thea Beckman's Dutch original into English, I decided to try the novel in German (to see if <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u> and Helmut Goeb's translation would be a better and more enjoyable reading fit for me). <br /><br />And yes indeed, <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u> is in my humble opinion very much vastly superior translation-wise to <u>Crusade in Jeans</u>. For while I have had some issues with Thea Beckman's general themes and attitudes (as they are presented in <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u>), Helmut Goeb's translation has definitely felt to and for me as though I am reading not just a rendering from Dutch to German but a well written, readable and relatable story in and of itself (and indeed, I have also been able to actually and in fact both finish and appreciate <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u>, whereas the writing style and pacing of <u>Crusade in Jeans</u> turned me off to such an extent that I ended up not even being able to complete the latter before <u>Crusade in Jeans</u> needed to go back to my local library's interlibrary loan department and I have also never felt like making a further request for it). <br /><br />However and that having been said (and while <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u> has certainly and generally been a very much enjoyable personal reading experience), I also have to admit (as already alluded to above) that some of the thematics and contents of <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u> (and by extension also and of course Thea Beckman's Dutch original of <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u>) make me both a bit uncomfortable and also a bit annoyed from a historic reality point of view. And no, it is actually not so much the cases of anachronisms present in <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u> (and its translations) that tend to bother me (although indeed they can be a trifle frustrating), as my main issue is with the in the novel generally presented and featured attitude of supposed superiority of the 20th century and that main protagonist Rolf is somehow and far too often placed on some almost unassailable golden pedestal (that he is the almost pre-ordained leader of the children's crusade and not so much due to his personality or his learned skills but simply because at least in my opinion, according to the author, according to Thea Beckman, Rolf is a saviour type and a hero, someone who is basically often all-knowing due to the simple fact that he has time traveled into the Middle Ages from the 20th century and that conversely, Niclas/Nicholas, the original "leader" of the children's crusade, is simply not leadership material because he is both of the Middle Ages and well, also just a peasant, just an animal herder and easily duped by the false monks because of this). <br /><br />And while yes, I have appreciated reading about Thea Beckman's (and by extension translator Helmut Goeb's) vision of the Middle Ages in <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u> and do very much appreciate that the inhabitants presented are generally depicted as not just dirty and unhygienic subhumans, personally I do very much kind of chafe at how glowingly positive and often very much superior to basically almost everyone Rolf is often portrayed within the pages of <u>Kreuzzug in Jeans</u> (probably a symptom and sign of what I tend to label as in particular 1970s optimism of the 20th century being a time of and for advancement and as such much better in and of itself than previous, than prior centuries, but as a 21st century reader that kind of an often holier and better than thou attitude and viewpoint can and does get a trifle frustrating and stale and makes especially Rolf at times appear as much too good to be true), not to mention that I also have found that entire scenario of Rolf meeting up with Leonardo Fibonacci as a student and actually teaching him Arabic numbers a trifle groan-worthy (because it sure makes it seem as though Thea Beckman is basically kind of claiming that the Middle Ages need rescuing and help from the present and that a famous mathematician like Leonardo Fibonacci can only obtain the mathematical knowledge for which he is famous from a time travelling 20th century teenaged boy, and sorry, that kind of makes me think of Erich von Däniken's worldview that great civilisations such as the Incas supposedly needed aliens to teach them how to thrive and become advanced).</span>
  <a data-text-id="13454398599380254794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2750591580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2750591580" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2750591580?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780684143996" href="/book/show/1462254.Crusade_In_Jeans">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Middle Grade &amp; Teen Readers Who Enjoy Time-Slip Adventure and/or Historical Fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fantasy">childrens-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-translations">childrens-translations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=medieval-europe">medieval-europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=dutch-children">dutch-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2750591580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18398450260567673345">Originally published in 1973, as <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u>, this classic Dutch children's novel follows the story of Rudolph Hefting, a twentieth-century boy who finds himself transported back in time to the year 1212, and caught up in the events of the fabled Children's Crusade. Not sure that he can ever return to his own time, Dolf, together with Leonardo Fibonacci of Pisa - the young mathematics student he meets upon the road - decides to accompany the poorly organized crusade, hoping to hel</span>
  <span id="freeText18398450260567673345" style="display:none">Originally published in 1973, as <u>Kruistocht in spijkerbroek</u>, this classic Dutch children's novel follows the story of Rudolph Hefting, a twentieth-century boy who finds himself transported back in time to the year 1212, and caught up in the events of the fabled Children's Crusade. Not sure that he can ever return to his own time, Dolf, together with Leonardo Fibonacci of Pisa - the young mathematics student he meets upon the road - decides to accompany the poorly organized crusade, hoping to help the children survive. So begins a monumental journey south, across the Karwendel range of the Alps, toward Genoa, and the sea.<br /><br />The children believe that their nominal leader, Nicholas the shepherd boy, has had a vision from God, and (when they come to Genoa) will divide the sea, and lead them to the White City of Jerusalem, there to put to flight the Saracens. Dolf, with his twentieth-century skepticism, believes otherwise, but finds that he must accommodate himself - in public, anyway - to the customs and beliefs of the times. When treachery is revealed, and the true purpose of the crusade becomes clear, will Dolf, Leonardo, and their group of dedicated friends, be able to save the children from a terrible fate? And even if they do... what then?<br /><br /><u>Crusade in Jeans</u> is not a book without flaw. To begin with, I sometimes found the language a little awkward, although I understand, from reading reviews by Dutch-speakers, that this is owing to the poor translation. It irked me, moreover, to see that the translator is not listed anywhere on (or in) the book! I also found some of the "history" questionable. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibonacci" rel="nofollow noopener">Leonardo Fibonacci</a>, for instance, would have been forty-two years old, in 1212, rather than a young student, and would already have published his famous <i>Liber Abaci</i> (in 1202), which did so much to bring Arabic numerals (to which Dolph supposedly exposes him, in the novel) to Europe. Then, of course, there is the question of the Children's Crusade itself - an apocryphal event (events?), now largely discredited by historians.<br /><br />Still, Beckman's theory of how reports of such an event may have been started, made for fascinating reading. More importantly, her general grasp for the times - the importance attached to social class and position, the omnipresence of faith, both in internal decision-making, and overt practice, the appalling ignorance of geography, but surprisingly good hygiene (Dolf had always been taught that all people in the Middle Ages were dirty) - was top notch, and I came away from the story with the feeling that, like Dolf, I had truly stepped back in time. I also came away with a true attachment to the characters, and a desire to know more. I wanted to know what happened with Leonardo and Maria, later on - did they ever figure out where Dolf came from? I wanted to learn more about the boy who took Dolph's place, in the (then) present, and what happened to both of them, when they returned to their "correct" times.<br /><br />This attachment points to another great strength, in Beckman's narrative: her character-building, and engaging storytelling style. This wasn't just historical fiction, or time-slip novel, but an exciting adventure, peopled with characters I had come to love. I had no idea how it would all be resolved - or if it <i>would</i> be resolved, in terms of Dolf returning to his own time - but was completely engrossed in the here and now: how would the children get across the Alps? How would Dolph rescue the fifty little crusaders kidnapped by the knights of Count Romhild of Scharnitz? What would happen, once the sea refused to part? <br /><br />I was riveted! It's a shame that this is the only one of Thea Beckman's many children's books to be translated, thus far! I would definitely read more, if I had the chance!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18398450260567673345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1901361088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1901361088" />
    <a title="Romi || Romi Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10503669-romi-romi-reads"><img alt="Romi || Romi Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586699636p2/10503669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1901361088?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romi || Romi Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romi || Romi Reads" href="/user/show/10503669-romi-romi-reads">Romi || Romi Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10503669-romi-romi-reads?shelf=in-my-possession">in-my-possession</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1901361088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1938783425074129233">How lovely it was to revisit a childhood story! I love history, but somehow it wasn't the class I got the best grades in. I think it's more the stories that interest me! Like Crusade in Jeans (or Kruistocht in spijkerbroek). The main character Dolf says at one point something along the way of that you get to know all about the rich "important" men of history, but not so much about the "normal" human. And those are who interest me the most actually! It was also a period in time I didn't get to kn</span>
  <span id="freeText1938783425074129233" style="display:none">How lovely it was to revisit a childhood story! I love history, but somehow it wasn't the class I got the best grades in. I think it's more the stories that interest me! Like Crusade in Jeans (or Kruistocht in spijkerbroek). The main character Dolf says at one point something along the way of that you get to know all about the rich "important" men of history, but not so much about the "normal" human. And those are who interest me the most actually! It was also a period in time I didn't get to know much about in history class, so it's really refreshing to fill in the gaps a bit. The Children's Crusade really did take place in 1212, but of course, not in the way it's portrayed in the book. Still, Crusade in Jeans gives the reader the most important messages of living in that age across - the differences between the rich and the poor, Christian faith and just how different the world was back then, compared to the one we live in now! <br /><br />I really lived for every single character of the book, except for maybe one - the bad guy. I won't tell you their name, because that would spoil the fun and this story is really worth the read as it's slowly building up to its climax! One of the only things that bugged me was maybe that Dolf was a little too clever for his age. He knew things I definitely didn't know at 16 or didn't want to know, because I was too busy with hating the world like any other teenager. Another thing was the ending - it was kind of open! I just wanted to keep on reading (so actually not really a bad thing after all ;)). The story just wasn't over for me! <br /><br />I read this book in Dutch and the language was kind of old fashioned. I don't think the young generation of today can relate to Dolf that much, but then again, the story will never get old! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1938783425074129233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1951540286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1951540286" />
    <a title="Travis Berketa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8307433-travis-berketa"><img alt="Travis Berketa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513776499p2/8307433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1951540286?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis Berketa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis Berketa" href="/user/show/8307433-travis-berketa">Travis Berketa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781935954071" href="/book/show/11129634-crusade-in-jeans">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1951540286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10318390719750836124">Maybe it was the fact that it was written back in 1973, but I found this story a bit hard to believe. Now I know that it's not a true story, however there were too many instances where I felt the reader needed to stretch their imagination in order to accept it.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Firstly, the whole time travel scenario; if a 15-year-old boy said that they would be willing to go off in a time machine that has never been tested on humans, I doubt that any scientist would agree to it, no matter how man</span></span>
  <span id="freeText10318390719750836124" style="display:none">Maybe it was the fact that it was written back in 1973, but I found this story a bit hard to believe. Now I know that it's not a true story, however there were too many instances where I felt the reader needed to stretch their imagination in order to accept it.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Firstly, the whole time travel scenario; if a 15-year-old boy said that they would be willing to go off in a time machine that has never been tested on humans, I doubt that any scientist would agree to it, no matter how many times the child pleaded. They didn't even explain things to the parents prior to him going, which raises the questions about their moral/ethical codes.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Once the reader gets their head around this, they are transported into the Middle Ages in thirteenth century France, where their understandings of humanity are further tested. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Now, I can kind of believe that a 15-year-old boy might get excited about being sent back to the past, but to run up to a fight where <i>"two men on horseback had attacked a third man, on foot, who was wielding a cudgel and shouting"</i> to me seems a little too far fetched. Furthermore, his ability to communicate with the people from this time, where he understands them and they understand him, is also questionable.<br /><br />But the most significant area where this story falls apart is where Rudolf Hefting attempts to return to the rock that he landed in order to return home, but is shoved off and is then stranded in the past. Dolf's reaction to this is virtually one of absolute acceptance, so much so that he picks himself up and joins a Children's Crusade that is passing through at the time. How is it that a fifteen year old boy would not be in tears and fearing for his life when faced with the possibility of never returning back to his time period and never seeing his family and friends again? I found this whole part of the story very unrealistic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Although, upon accepting these initial "plot-holes", the adventure that follows is quite good. There are still many parts where I found myself questioning whether a fifteen-year-old would behave in this way and also questioned the experiences that Dolf apparently had in his fifteen years of life. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The reader is meant to believe that a fifteen-year-old who has only just been brought into the Middle Ages would know the ways of the people in this time (with only a few hiccups). Dolf apparently knew the landscape, as though the world had not really changed (other than possibly a few roads being missing); his sense of direction was impeccable. Dolf stood up to the leaders of the crusade and thrust himself in the leadership role without any real reservations; even though the majority of people following him were children, he still took on adults without any real repercussions.<br /><br />The most puzzling scene I thought was when Dolf decided that he should come up with a plan to infiltrate a castle in order to rescue some children that were taken by the lord of that castle. How could a mere child have such tactical understanding that he would be able to infiltrate a castle full of soldiers and rescue the prisoners? He was not a military man (boy) and, as far as I know, he was not brought up in a military family - so for Dolf to devise such a plan would be near impossible to believe. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There are many more areas in the book that I question, but have not written up in this review.<br /><br />That said, once you get your head around all of the remarkable things that Dolf seems to be able to conquer and achieve, the book is entertaining and is a decent read for teenagers (who may not question the realism of it as much as adults).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10318390719750836124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789082969528" href="/book/show/43900049-kruistocht-in-spijkerbroek">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=dutch">dutch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=1950-1974">1950-1974</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3124102877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4045116225023528948">English title: <u>Crusade in Jeans</u><br/><br/>A classic Dutch children's book. I thought I had read it when I was a child, but nothing sounded familiar, so maybe not?<br/><br/>The book is about a boy, Dolf, who is transported to the middle ages with a time machine. The plan was for him to be there for a few hours, but things went wrong and he ends up stuck in Germany in the year 1212. He joins a children's crusade to Jerusalem and quickly finds his place between 8000 children. <br/><br/>So one thing you should know when you are g</span>
  <span id="freeText4045116225023528948" style="display:none">English title: <u>Crusade in Jeans</u><br /><br />A classic Dutch children's book. I thought I had read it when I was a child, but nothing sounded familiar, so maybe not?<br /><br />The book is about a boy, Dolf, who is transported to the middle ages with a time machine. The plan was for him to be there for a few hours, but things went wrong and he ends up stuck in Germany in the year 1212. He joins a children's crusade to Jerusalem and quickly finds his place between 8000 children. <br /><br />So one thing you should know when you are going to read this book is that it is written in 1973. So some things that are being said in the story would never end up in (children's) books nowadays. Also, A LOT of children die in this book. And with a lot I mean they are dropping like flies. <br /><br />I like that it teaches you about the middle ages and I haven't checked all the facts Beckman has written in this book, but I assume she has done her research. I know that the crusade they talked about really existed and it was called a children's crusade, but apparently there were also a lot of grownups in the real crusade. <br /><br />It was fun to have read this book (again?) and reading it through the eyes of an adult is always a different experience. Not sure if children would still enjoy this nowadays.<br /><br /><b>3 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Read with Fanatieke Nederlandse Lezers for the month January 2020,</i> A childhood favorite that would still be fun today.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4045116225023528948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9261734951556664418">Came across one of the favourite books from my childhood going through boxes of books in the attic, which I have yet to move to the UK. Reading this now, I can see how messy and rushed the beginning is; no time is wasted jumping into the 13th century crusade.   <span id="freeText9261734951556664418" style="display:none">Came across one of the favourite books from my childhood going through boxes of books in the attic, which I have yet to move to the UK. Reading this now, I can see how messy and rushed the beginning is; no time is wasted jumping into the 13th century crusade. Once having time-travelled there, Dolf struggles for what appears to be a few days learning the "language" Diets; even the 8,000 German children who came from various areas must've spoken various dialects, variations of this unstandardized language. If you look beyond the plot holes, the implausibility of the speed of things, this is a captivating read (even as an adult!) and I understand why it was a favourite of mine.</span>

<div id="review_20440464" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20440464" />
    <a title="Katharine (Ventureadlaxre)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1094570-katharine-ventureadlaxre"><img alt="Katharine (Ventureadlaxre)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419414955p2/1094570.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katharine (Ventureadlaxre)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katharine (Ventureadlaxre)" href="/user/show/1094570-katharine-ventureadlaxre">Katharine (Ventureadlaxre)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781886910263" href="/book/show/974324.Crusade_in_Jeans">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1094570-katharine-ventureadlaxre?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1094570-katharine-ventureadlaxre?shelf=read-2008">read-2008</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20440464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12145668771592389536"><i>Crusade in Jeans (1973) is a children's novel written by Thea Beckman. It contains a fictional account of the children's crusade of 1212, as witnessed by Rudolph Wega, a boy from the 20th century. The original Dutch title is Kruistocht in spijkerbroek.<br/><br/>Rudolph Wega is a sixteen year-old who volunteers for an experiment with a time machine. The experiment goes well, but through an accident Rudolph is stranded in the 13th century. He saves the life of Leonardo Fibonacci, without realizing who he is</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12145668771592389536" style="display:none"><i>Crusade in Jeans (1973) is a children's novel written by Thea Beckman. It contains a fictional account of the children's crusade of 1212, as witnessed by Rudolph Wega, a boy from the 20th century. The original Dutch title is Kruistocht in spijkerbroek.<br /><br />Rudolph Wega is a sixteen year-old who volunteers for an experiment with a time machine. The experiment goes well, but through an accident Rudolph is stranded in the 13th century. He saves the life of Leonardo Fibonacci, without realizing who he is, and teaches him Arabic numerals. Together they join the German Children's Crusade, and through his modern-day knowledge, Rudolph manages to save a lot of children from horrible fates. However, his knowledge also leads to accusations of witchcraft.<br /><br />In the book, two slavers delude a group of children into coming with them with stories of how the innocent shall liberate Jerusalem. Their actual intent is to sell them for profit. With the aid of his twentieth-century knowledge and skepticism, and the aid of a "magical" device or two (such as a box of matches), the boy manages to keep most of the children alive and eventually gets them to safety.</i><br /><br /><br />I was drawn in by this book to a dangerous level. I was currently in Tokyo at the time and kept bumping into busy people rushing to the train because I couldn't put the book down.<br /><br />It captures a bit of wonder that is sometimes lost in the serious books of today. It's quite bittersweet, and you half expect the ending but then you're also kind of surprised by it too. I loved this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12145668771592389536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It always maybe want to read a story about his life after returning to his own time.</span>

<div id="review_2762728865" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2762728865" />
    <a title="RH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77151488-rh"><img alt="RH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544258733p2/77151488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2762728865?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RH" href="/user/show/77151488-rh">RH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781886910263" href="/book/show/974324.Crusade_in_Jeans">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2762728865&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2762728865" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3677904895076027237">In the 20th century, a sixteen-year-old boy, Dolf Wega van Amstelveen, is sent back in time to the Middle Ages. Instead of a knight tournament he wanted to witness in Montgivray, he ends up in Speyer (Germany). Without a way of returning to his own century, he is forced to join a crusade of children, who hope to scare the Saracens and save Jerusalem. With his twentieth-century knowledge, Dolf manages to organize the mess of eight thousand children into a well-structured organization, and forms t</span>
  <span id="freeText3677904895076027237" style="display:none">In the 20th century, a sixteen-year-old boy, Dolf Wega van Amstelveen, is sent back in time to the Middle Ages. Instead of a knight tournament he wanted to witness in Montgivray, he ends up in Speyer (Germany). Without a way of returning to his own century, he is forced to join a crusade of children, who hope to scare the Saracens and save Jerusalem. With his twentieth-century knowledge, Dolf manages to organize the mess of eight thousand children into a well-structured organization, and forms teams to catch fish, hunt for prey, make shoes and protect the youth. He saves more than fifty children captured the day before. He also convinces the leaders to change the route as traveling over the mountains will kill many. Their journey takes longer, but is saver now, the loss of life less significant. Close to Genua the real purpose of the journey becomes clear when the monks traveling with them reveal that the children are about to be shipped to Africa, where they can serve as slaves. The money they were promised was their reason to organize the crusade and trick children to travel with them. The leading monk is killed by angry children and the army finds it way further down into Italy, while about one thousand return to their homeland. The road ends in Bari and Brindisi, without a way to continue their trip to Jerusalem. Their numbers were reduced over months to fifteen hundred. The remaining children find work, become citizens and live their life in their new-found places. It is here a box is sent from the future with a message, the possibility of a return to the future. Upon his return, after all these months, with all these children and all they had to do to survive, Dolf is finally able to see his parents' faces ago in the century he belongs.<br /><br />This book is clearly written for children because whatever happens, hero Dolf solves the problems and makes the day. Things happen with ease and no problem seems to get the upper hand. A nice book to have read once, but not one worth reading again. On the other hand, seeing this book's target group it is well written into an exciting story. That being said this book might get children interested a little more in history and the Middle Ages in particular.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3677904895076027237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_760439749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/760439749" />
    <a title="Marietje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14714035-marietje"><img alt="Marietje" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/760439749?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marietje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marietje" href="/user/show/14714035-marietje">Marietje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer760439749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8807711851994409845">I read this book in Dutch in the1970's when I studied to be a children's librarian. Recently, almost 40 years later (of which 30 years spent in the USA), I decided to read the English translation, called "Crusade in Jeans". I even vaguely remember attending reading by Thea Beckman, but I don't know which book. One of the main reasons the book gained so much acclaim 40 years ago, was Beckman's use of the Dutch language. Her writing was crisp, clear and simple. The story was told in a very direct </span>
  <span id="freeText8807711851994409845" style="display:none">I read this book in Dutch in the1970's when I studied to be a children's librarian. Recently, almost 40 years later (of which 30 years spent in the USA), I decided to read the English translation, called "Crusade in Jeans". I even vaguely remember attending reading by Thea Beckman, but I don't know which book. One of the main reasons the book gained so much acclaim 40 years ago, was Beckman's use of the Dutch language. Her writing was crisp, clear and simple. The story was told in a very direct way. Despite the fact that this translation was not bad, I missed some of the mood Beckman created with her use of language.<br /><br />Over the years I have become a skeptic of time travel in children's books. I have become sensitive to the mode of "teleportation" and the logic behind it. I have to remember that in 1973 we stood at the beginning of writing specifically for young adults, and also that technology was much less advanced. In 1973 no cell phones could time travel to the Middle Ages. I discovered that in this book, the way the journey to the past happens is irrelevant. What is relevant is how a modern teenager thinks, feels and acts when he lands in the middle of a medieval children's crusade. This Beckman describes very clearly without getting into too much psychological detail, especially when Dolf is accused of being a heretic. <br /><br />There was one loose end that did not get tied up: what happen to the 13th century boy, who got sent to the twentieth century? Was he sent back in time? Did he decided to stay in the 20th century? I wish Beckman was still alive. She could have told us.<br /><br />Do not watch the movie of this book which came out about a year ago, it disgusting and does not do the book justice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8807711851994409845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35533168-gilraens?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1869946460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13698631795861563662">This book is a very very poor translation of Kruistocht in spijkerbroek. I still gave it two stars as it is my most favourite book from groiwng up. But the translation leaves a book so well loved butchered on its pages. I was almost traumatized reading this translation.<br/><br/>Major parts of the original are missing, people are missing, events are devoid of the depth that are in the original. A prime example of how a translation can go so very very terribly wrong</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3117197933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3117197933" />
    <a title="Karla Conchas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45931360-karla-conchas"><img alt="Karla Conchas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583899469p2/45931360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3117197933?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla Conchas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla Conchas" href="/user/show/45931360-karla-conchas">Karla Conchas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781886910263" href="/book/show/974324.Crusade_in_Jeans">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3117197933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1553579550165824080">This was a really good read for sure. I saw the movie a long time ago, when I was nineteen or so, and I decided to read the book. Rudolf of amsterdam, as he so proudly likes to say to the medieval people he comes across (much to my amusement) finds himself trapped in medieval Europe after getting sent there by a group of scientists. He gets caught up in the children's crusade, as they are passing along his friend Leonardo, who he meets in a scuffle (I love this guy!), helps two sick and exhauste</span>
  <span id="freeText1553579550165824080" style="display:none">This was a really good read for sure. I saw the movie a long time ago, when I was nineteen or so, and I decided to read the book. Rudolf of amsterdam, as he so proudly likes to say to the medieval people he comes across (much to my amusement) finds himself trapped in medieval Europe after getting sent there by a group of scientists. He gets caught up in the children's crusade, as they are passing along his friend Leonardo, who he meets in a scuffle (I love this guy!), helps two sick and exhausted little ones ride on his donkey. From then on and throughout the rest of the book you read about the various adventures and trials this large group of children face. Dolf sort of takes charge of the group and brings it together in a more organized way with concern for the welfare of the children. The two scumbag priests are a real piece of work. It was funny at parts when Rudolf would try to relate to the medieval people's understanding of things or when he would try to explain things or things the medieval people would say. You fall in love with the characters. For me I loved little Caralous and Leonardo the most. I don't know some people might think it's boring but I liked it. It's a good time travel story and I've always loved a good time travel book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1553579550165824080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen Dooren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen Dooren" href="/user/show/49566607-ellen-dooren">Ellen Dooren</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2747729999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11498484819000497937">First thoughts:<br/>It is a Dutch children's classic, but I have never read it before. I only saw the movie when I was younger. I didn't remember too much from the movie, so I could go into it without too many expectations and prior knowledge.<br/><br/>The language is really old fashioned and not at all how a children's book would be written nowadays. From time to time this makes the main character a bit more unbelievable, since his thoughts and the things that he says are formulated in a really old fashioned </span>
  <span id="freeText11498484819000497937" style="display:none">First thoughts:<br />It is a Dutch children's classic, but I have never read it before. I only saw the movie when I was younger. I didn't remember too much from the movie, so I could go into it without too many expectations and prior knowledge.<br /><br />The language is really old fashioned and not at all how a children's book would be written nowadays. From time to time this makes the main character a bit more unbelievable, since his thoughts and the things that he says are formulated in a really old fashioned and adultly manner. <br />Apart from that, it was an exciting story and I regret not reading it when I was younger. I would have loved it.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mXwCIH+dhwgvbcIpZd3rHrQRv/0RaGiYeD84K2tBD8hb8dCt9/pMa8SVhUOgpknp+8AIb4lHiKtwXciGyyO6LA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

De hoofdpersoon, de 14-jarige Arnold, is geen verzetsheld. Hij is zelfs niet tegen de Duitsers! Arnolds vader is ervan overtuigd dat bij volk en vaderland het beste dient door het nieuwe bewind te steunen. Hij is dus lid van de NSB en Arnold van de jeugdstorm. Arnolds klasgenoten vinden dat niet zo vanzelfsprekend. Hij wordt voortdurend gepest en getreiterd, soms afgetuigd. Maar Arnold ziet niet in waarom bij \'fout\' zou zijn, want hij gelooft heilig in wat de partij propageert. Hij helpt Duitsers en geeft klasgenoten aan, ook al zit dat laatste hem niet lekker. Zo speelt hij de rol die zijn vader hem voorschrijft. Dan ontdekt Arnold dat het meisje op wie hij verliefd is ondergronds werk doet. En hij besluit tegen alle orders in te zwijgen. Nu komt bij helemaal alleen te staan: thuis kan hij geen open kaart spelen en zijn klasgenoten vertrouwen hem tóch niet.               e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_88387').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4357136653061280184">Thea Beckman (1923-2004) was born in Rotterdam. She began writing in 1947, but it was not until her children were grown that she devoted herself to writing full time. <i>Crusade in Jeans</i> was first published in 1973. It became an overnight success, making her one of the most popular authors of juvenile books in the Netherlands. Ms. Beckman is fascinated by history and wrote books about many historical</span>
  <span id="freeText4357136653061280184" style="display:none">Thea Beckman (1923-2004) was born in Rotterdam. She began writing in 1947, but it was not until her children were grown that she devoted herself to writing full time. <i>Crusade in Jeans</i> was first published in 1973. It became an overnight success, making her one of the most popular authors of juvenile books in the Netherlands. Ms. Beckman is fascinated by history and wrote books about many historical periods.</span>
